floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <img src=\textbackslash{}"/icons/ubuntu{-}logo.png\textbackslash{}" alt=\textbackslash{}"Ubuntu Logo\textbackslash{}" class=\textbackslash{}"floating\_element\textbackslash{}"/>\textbackslash{}n        <span class=\textbackslash{}"floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          Apache2 Ubuntu Default Page\textbackslash{}n        </span>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n<!{-}{-}      <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_grey\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          TABLE OF CONTENTS\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#about\textbackslash{}">About</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#changes\textbackslash{}">Changes</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#scope\textbackslash{}">Scope</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#files\textbackslash{}">Config files</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n{-}{-}>\textbackslash{}n      <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_red\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"about\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n          It works!\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \textbackslash{}n                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\textbackslash{}n                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\textbackslash{}n                href=\textbackslash{}"https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2\textbackslash{}"\textbackslash{}n                rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\textbackslash{}n                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n    </div>\textbackslash{}n    <div Page\textbackslash{}n        </span>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n<!{-}{-}      <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_grey\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          TABLE OF CONTENTS\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a  </div>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n{-}{-}>\textbackslash{}n      <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_red\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"about\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n          It works!\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \textbackslash{}n                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\textbackslash{}n                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#scope\textbackslash{}">Scope</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#files\textbackslash{}">Config files</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n{-}{-}>\textbackslash{}n      <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_red\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"about\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n          It works!\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \textbackslash{}n                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\textbackslash{}n                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\textbackslash{}n                href=\textbackslash{}"https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2\textbackslash{}"\textbackslash{}n                rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\textbackslash{}n                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <img src=\textbackslash{}"/icons/ubuntu{-}logo.png\textbackslash{}" alt=\textbackslash{}"Ubuntu Logo\textbackslash{}" class=\textbackslash{}"floating\_element\textbackslash{}"/>\textbackslash{}n        <span class=\textbackslash{}"floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          Apache2 Ubuntu Default Page\textbackslash{}n        </span>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n<!{-}{-}      <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_grey\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          TABLE OF CONTENTS\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#about\textbackslash{}">About</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#changes\textbackslash{}">Changes</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#scope\textbackslash{}">Scope</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a href=\textbackslash{}"\#files\textbackslash{}">Config files</a>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n{-}{-}>\textbackslash{}n      <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_red\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"about\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n          It works!\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \textbackslash{}n                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\textbackslash{}n                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\textbackslash{}n                href=\textbackslash{}"https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2\textbackslash{}"\textbackslash{}n                rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\textbackslash{}n                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n    </div>\textbackslash{}n    <div floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <img src=\textbackslash{}"/icons/ubuntu{-}logo.png\textbackslash{}" alt=\textbackslash{}"Ubuntu Logo\textbackslash{}" Page\textbackslash{}n        </span>\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n<!{-}{-}      <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_grey\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          TABLE OF CONTENTS\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <a floating\_element\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header section\_header\_red\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"about\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n          It works!\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \textbackslash{}n                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\textbackslash{}n                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\textbackslash{}n                href=\textbackslash{}"https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2\textbackslash{}"\textbackslash{}n                rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\textbackslash{}n                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n      </div>\textbackslash{}n    </div>\textbackslash{}n    <div Ubuntu Apache\textbackslash{}n                packaging is derived.\textbackslash{}n                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\textbackslash{}n                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\textbackslash{}n                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\textbackslash{}n                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\textbackslash{}n                maintenance.\textbackslash{}n                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"changes\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Configuration Overview\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\textbackslash{}n                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\textbackslash{}n                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\textbackslash{}n                <b>fully documented in\textbackslash{}n                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\textbackslash{}n                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\textbackslash{}n                found by accessing the <a href=\textbackslash{}"/manual\textbackslash{}">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\textbackslash{}n                package was installed on this server.\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <pre>\textbackslash{}n/etc/apache2/\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} apache2.conf\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       |{-}{-} *.load\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\textbackslash{}n|       `{-}{-} *.conf\textbackslash{}n          </pre>\textbackslash{}n          <ul>\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\textbackslash{}n                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\textbackslash{}n                           files when starting up the web server.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\textbackslash{}n                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\textbackslash{}n                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\textbackslash{}n                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\textbackslash{}n                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           They are activated by symlinking available\textbackslash{}n                           configuration files from their respective\textbackslash{}n                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\textbackslash{}n                           by using our helpers\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enmod,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dismod,\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2ensite,\textbackslash{}n                                a2dissite,\textbackslash{}n                            </tt>\textbackslash{}n                                and\textbackslash{}n                           <tt>\textbackslash{}n                                a2enconf,\textbackslash{}n                                a2disconf\textbackslash{}n                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n                        <li>\textbackslash{}n                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\textbackslash{}n                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\textbackslash{}n                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\textbackslash{}n                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\textbackslash{}n                           default configuration.\textbackslash{}n                        </li>\textbackslash{}n          </ul>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <div id=\textbackslash{}"docroot\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Document Roots\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\textbackslash{}n                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\textbackslash{}n                <a href=\textbackslash{}"http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html\textbackslash{}" rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">public\_html</a>\textbackslash{}n                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\textbackslash{}n                applications). If your site is using a web document root\textbackslash{}n                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\textbackslash{}n                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n            <p>\textbackslash{}n                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\textbackslash{}n                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\textbackslash{}n                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\textbackslash{}n            </p>\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"section\_header\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <div id=\textbackslash{}"bugs\textbackslash{}"></div>\textbackslash{}n                Reporting Problems\textbackslash{}n        </div>\textbackslash{}n        <div class=\textbackslash{}"content\_section\_text\textbackslash{}">\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\textbackslash{}n                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\textbackslash{}n                href=\textbackslash{}"https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2\textbackslash{}"\textbackslash{}n                rel=\textbackslash{}"nofollow\textbackslash{}">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n          <p>\textbackslash{}n                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\textbackslash{}n                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\textbackslash{}n          </p>\textbackslash{}n   div.validator \{\newline%
  \}\newline%
    </style>\newline%
  </head>\newline%
  <body>\newline%
    <div class="main\_page">\newline%
      <div class="page\_header floating\_element">\newline%
        <img src="/icons/ubuntu{-}logo.png" alt="Ubuntu Logo" class="floating\_element"/>\newline%
        <span class="floating\_element">\newline%
          Apache2 Ubuntu Default Page\newline%
        </span>\newline%
      </div>\newline%
<!{-}{-}      <div class="table\_of\_contents floating\_element">\newline%
        <div class="section\_header section\_header\_grey">\newline%
          TABLE OF CONTENTS\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element">\newline%
          <a href="\#about">About</a>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element">\newline%
          <a href="\#changes">Changes</a>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element">\newline%
          <a href="\#scope">Scope</a>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="table\_of\_contents\_item floating\_element">\newline%
          <a href="\#files">Config files</a>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
      </div>\newline%
{-}{-}>\newline%
      <div class="content\_section floating\_element">\newline%
\newline%
\newline%
        <div class="section\_header section\_header\_red">\newline%
          <div id="about"></div>\newline%
          It works!\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="content\_section\_text">\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                This is the default welcome page used to test the correct \newline%
                operation of the Apache2 server after installation on Ubuntu systems.\newline%
                It is based on the equivalent page on Debian, from which the Ubuntu Apache\newline%
                packaging is derived.\newline%
                If you can read this page, it means that the Apache HTTP server installed at\newline%
                this site is working properly. You should <b>replace this file</b> (located at\newline%
                <tt>/var/www/html/index.html</tt>) before continuing to operate your HTTP server.\newline%
          </p>\newline%
\newline%
\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                If you are a normal user of this web site and don't know what this page is\newline%
                about, this probably means that the site is currently unavailable due to\newline%
                maintenance.\newline%
                If the problem persists, please contact the site's administrator.\newline%
          </p>\newline%
\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="section\_header">\newline%
          <div id="changes"></div>\newline%
                Configuration Overview\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="content\_section\_text">\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                Ubuntu's Apache2 default configuration is different from the\newline%
                upstream default configuration, and split into several files optimized for\newline%
                interaction with Ubuntu tools. The configuration system is\newline%
                <b>fully documented in\newline%
                /usr/share/doc/apache2/README.Debian.gz</b>. Refer to this for the full\newline%
                documentation. Documentation for the web server itself can be\newline%
                found by accessing the <a href="/manual">manual</a> if the <tt>apache2{-}doc</tt>\newline%
                package was installed on this server.\newline%
\newline%
          </p>\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                The configuration layout for an Apache2 web server installation on Ubuntu systems is as follows:\newline%
          </p>\newline%
          <pre>\newline%
/etc/apache2/\newline%
|{-}{-} apache2.conf\newline%
|       `{-}{-}  ports.conf\newline%
|{-}{-} mods{-}enabled\newline%
|       |{-}{-} *.load\newline%
|       `{-}{-} *.conf\newline%
|{-}{-} conf{-}enabled\newline%
|       `{-}{-} *.conf\newline%
|{-}{-} sites{-}enabled\newline%
|       `{-}{-} *.conf\newline%
          </pre>\newline%
          <ul>\newline%
                        <li>\newline%
                           <tt>apache2.conf</tt> is the main configuration\newline%
                           file. It puts the pieces together by including all remaining configuration\newline%
                           files when starting up the web server.\newline%
                        </li>\newline%
\newline%
                        <li>\newline%
                           <tt>ports.conf</tt> is always included from the\newline%
                           main configuration file. It is used to determine the listening ports for\newline%
                           incoming connections, and this file can be customized anytime.\newline%
                        </li>\newline%
\newline%
                        <li>\newline%
                           Configuration files in the <tt>mods{-}enabled/</tt>,\newline%
                           <tt>conf{-}enabled/</tt> and <tt>sites{-}enabled/</tt> directories contain\newline%
                           particular configuration snippets which manage modules, global configuration\newline%
                           fragments, or virtual host configurations, respectively.\newline%
                        </li>\newline%
\newline%
                        <li>\newline%
                           They are activated by symlinking available\newline%
                           configuration files from their respective\newline%
                           *{-}available/ counterparts. These should be managed\newline%
                           by using our helpers\newline%
                           <tt>\newline%
                                a2enmod,\newline%
                                a2dismod,\newline%
                           </tt>\newline%
                           <tt>\newline%
                                a2ensite,\newline%
                                a2dissite,\newline%
                            </tt>\newline%
                                and\newline%
                           <tt>\newline%
                                a2enconf,\newline%
                                a2disconf\newline%
                           </tt>. See their respective man pages for detailed information.\newline%
                        </li>\newline%
\newline%
                        <li>\newline%
                           The binary is called apache2. Due to the use of\newline%
                           environment variables, in the default configuration, apache2 needs to be\newline%
                           started/stopped with <tt>/etc/init.d/apache2</tt> or <tt>apache2ctl</tt>.\newline%
                           <b>Calling <tt>/usr/bin/apache2</tt> directly will not work</b> with the\newline%
                           default configuration.\newline%
                        </li>\newline%
          </ul>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
\newline%
        <div class="section\_header">\newline%
            <div id="docroot"></div>\newline%
                Document Roots\newline%
        </div>\newline%
\newline%
        <div class="content\_section\_text">\newline%
            <p>\newline%
                By default, Ubuntu does not allow access through the web browser to\newline%
                <em>any</em> file apart of those located in <tt>/var/www</tt>,\newline%
                <a href="http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.4/mod/mod\_userdir.html" rel="nofollow">public\_html</a>\newline%
                directories (when enabled) and <tt>/usr/share</tt> (for web\newline%
                applications). If your site is using a web document root\newline%
                located elsewhere (such as in <tt>/srv</tt>) you may need to whitelist your\newline%
                document root directory in <tt>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf</tt>.\newline%
            </p>\newline%
            <p>\newline%
                The default Ubuntu document root is <tt>/var/www/html</tt>. You\newline%
                can make your own virtual hosts under /var/www. This is different\newline%
                to previous releases which provides better security out of the box.\newline%
            </p>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
\newline%
        <div class="section\_header">\newline%
          <div id="bugs"></div>\newline%
                Reporting Problems\newline%
        </div>\newline%
        <div class="content\_section\_text">\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                Please use the <tt>ubuntu{-}bug</tt> tool to report bugs in the\newline%
                Apache2 package with Ubuntu. However, check <a\newline%
                href="https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/apache2"\newline%
                rel="nofollow">existing bug reports</a> before reporting a new bug.\newline%
          </p>\newline%
          <p>\newline%
                Please report bugs specific to modules (such as PHP and others)\newline%
                to respective packages, not to the web server itself.\newline%
          </p>\newline%
        </div>\newline%
\newline%
\newline%
\newline%
\newline%
      </div>\newline%
    </div>\newline%
    <div class="validator">\newline%
    </div>\newline%
  </body>\newline%
</html>\newline%
